However, there are significant gaps in coverage for connection-level lifecycle management, error handling, and edge cases. Key missing areas include:\n\n1. **Connection-level timeouts** (idle and max duration) - No dedicated tests exist for connection lifecycle events\n2. **Premature reset detection and drain logic** - Critical overload protection untested\n3. **Codec overload error handling** - Specific error path not covered separately from other codec errors\n4. **HTTP/1 safe drain mode** - Special max duration handling for HTTP/1 untested\n5. **Stream reset edge cases** - Various response flag combinations not tested\n6. **Request data size enforcement** - Filter chain buffer management edge cases\n7. **Stream validation error recovery** - Trailer validation and stream header errors\n\nThese gaps are HIGH risk because they involve critical resource management, overload protection, and error recovery paths that could cause proxy instability or security issues if bugs slip through.\n\n---\n\n## Coverage Gaps\n\n### Gap 1: Connection Idle Timeout Handler Not Tested\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~756-767\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: The `onIdleTimeout()` method handles connection-level idle timeouts. It has two distinct code paths:\n  1. If no codec exists: immediately close with FlushWrite\n  2. If codec exists and not draining: start drain sequence\n\n  No test currently exercises these paths to verify the timeout is handled correctly, drain sequence is initiated, or stats are incremented.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `ConnectionIdleTimeoutClosesConnectionWithoutActiveCodec`\n  - **Setup**:\n    - Create connection manager with idle timeout configured\n    - Do NOT send any data (keep codec uninitialized)\n    - Simulate idle timeout firing by calling `onIdleTimeout()`\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - Verify `downstream_cx_idle_timeout_` stat is incremented\n    - Verify `connection.close()` is called with `FlushWrite` mode\n    - Verify no drain sequence starts (codec is null)\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `ConnectionIdleTimeoutStartsDrainWithActiveCodec`\n  - **Setup**:\n    - Create connection manager with idle timeout configured\n    - Send initial HTTP request to create codec (HTTP/2)\n    - Simulate idle timeout firing\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - Verify `downstream_cx_idle_timeout_` stat is incremented\n    - Verify `codec->shutdownNotice()` is called\n    - Verify drain timer is enabled with configured drain timeout\n\n- **Why It Matters**: Idle timeout is a critical mechanism to prevent resource exhaustion from idle connections. Without this test, a regression could allow connections to hang indefinitely or fail to drain gracefully, accumulating memory and file descriptor exhaustion.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 2: Connection Duration Timeout Not Tested\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~769-788\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: The `onConnectionDurationTimeout()` method enforces maximum connection lifetime. It has three distinct paths:\n  1. No codec: immediate close with `FlushWrite`\n  2. Codec exists, HTTP/2+ protocol: start drain sequence\n  3. Codec exists, HTTP/1 with `http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration` flag: set `soft_drain_http1_` flag instead of draining\n\n  The HTTP/1 soft drain path (lines 778-787) is particularly critical but untested. This flag is used to gracefully close HTTP/1 connections without sending GOAWAY.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `ConnectionDurationTimeoutWithoutCodec`\n  - **Setup**:\n    - Create connection manager with max duration timeout configured\n    - Do NOT create codec (idle state)\n    - Simulate max duration timeout\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - Verify `downstream_cx_max_duration_reached_` stat is incremented\n    - Verify `connection.close()` called with `FlushWrite` and `DurationTimeout` response flag\n    - Verify response code details set to \"max_connection_duration\"\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `ConnectionDurationTimeoutWithHttp1SafeDrain`\n  - **Setup**:\n    - Enable `http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration()` config\n    - Create HTTP/1 codec\n    - Simulate max duration timeout\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - Verify `downstream_cx_http1_soft_drain_` stat is incremented\n    - Verify `soft_drain_http1_` flag is set to true\n    - Verify drain sequence is NOT started (no `shutdownNotice()` call)\n    - Verify connection remains open for current request completion\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `ConnectionDurationTimeoutWithHttp2StartsDrain`\n  - **Setup**:\n    - Create HTTP/2 codec\n    - Simulate max duration timeout\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - Verify `codec->shutdownNotice()` called\n    - Verify drain timer enabled\n    - Verify `soft_drain_http1_` is NOT set\n\n- **Why It Matters**: Max connection duration is essential for graceful restart and resource cycling. The HTTP/1 soft drain mode is a subtle but important optimization to avoid sending GOAWAY (which doesn't exist in HTTP/1). A regression here could cause ungraceful connection closures or break connection draining semantics.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: Premature Reset Detection and Drain Logic Untested\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~677-749 (isPrematureRstStream + maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets)\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: This code implements critical overload protection. When too many streams are reset prematurely (before receiving upstream response), the connection is drained to prevent upstream service overload.\n\n  Key untested paths:\n  1. `isPrematureRstStream()`: Determines if a stream was reset prematurely based on duration vs. configured threshold (line 677-698)\n  2. `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()`: Counts premature resets and drains connection when threshold exceeded (lines 702-749)\n     - Includes recursion prevention (lines 716-718)\n     - Two-tier threshold logic: total stream count vs. percentage of bad streams (lines 724-738)\n\n  The recursion prevention flag and threshold calculation logic are particularly subtle and error-prone.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `IsPrematureRstStreamDetectsQuickReset`\n  - **Setup**:\n    - Create stream with immediate reset (< 1 second)\n    - Stream has NO response code (never received upstream response)\n    - Set runtime minimum lifetime to 1 second\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - Verify `isPrematureRstStream()` returns true\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `IsPrematureRstStreamIgnoresSlowReset`\n  - **Setup**:\n    - Create stream that lives > threshold (e.g., 5 seconds)\n    - Even without response code, should not be considered premature\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - Verify `isPrematureRstStream()` returns false\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `MaybeDrainDueToPrematureResetsTriggersAtThreshold`\n  - **Setup**:\n    - Runtime: `PrematureResetTotalStreamCountKey = 10`, `PrematureResetMinStreamLifetimeSecondsKey = 1`\n    - Create 10 streams, all reset prematurely\n    - Call `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` after 10th reset\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - Verify `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` stat incremented\n    - Verify `connection.close()` called with `Abort` mode\n    - Verify `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` flag set (prevents recursion)\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `MaybeDrainDueToPrematureResetsPercentageThreshold`\n  - **Setup**:\n    - Runtime: `PrematureResetTotalStreamCountKey = 100`\n    - Create 100 streams total, 60 of which are premature\n    - Check: `60 * 2 = 120 > 100` means connection should drain\n    - Call drain check\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - Verify drain is triggered based on percentage logic\n    - Verify even if total < limit, high ratio of bad streams triggers drain\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `MaybeDrainDueToPrematureResetsRecursionPrevention`\n  - **Setup**:\n    - Set `drained_due_to_premature_resets_ = true`\n    - Call `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` multiple times\n  - **Assertions**:\n    - Verify no stack overflow\n    - Verify connection only drained once\n    - Verify flag prevents multiple drain sequences\n\n- **Why It Matters**: Premature reset detection is Envoy's first line of defense against upstream service overload attacks. If this logic is broken or regresses, a buggy or malicious client could trigger many premature resets and exhaust upstream resources. The subtle threshold logic and recursion prevention are easy to break during refactoring.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 4: Codec Overload Error Handling Not Tested\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~478-482 (handleCodecOverloadError)\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**: The `handleCodecOverloadError()` method specifically handles overload-related codec errors (e.g., codec rejected a request due to overload manager shedding load). Misclassifying overload errors as protocol errors could cause incorrect logging, monitoring, and alerting. The distinction matters for upstream metrics and admission control decisions.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 5: Stream Reset Response Flag Edge Cases Not Fully Tested\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~2070-2111 (onResetStream)\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**: The `onResetStream()` method sets response flags based on reset reason and encoder details. The distinction matters for upstream metrics and admission control decisions.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 5: Stream Reset Response Flag Edge Cases Not Fully Tested\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~2070-2111 (onResetStream)\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**: The `onResetStream()` method sets response flags based on reset reason and encoder details.
